
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Rewrite the polynomial equation in terms of symmetric sums of a, b, and c.'}, {'objective': 'Use the constraint a + b + c = 300 to relate and simplify the polynomial equation.'}, {'objective': 'Solve the resulting system to find all feasible values satisfying both the polynomial equation and the sum constraint.'}, {'objective': 'Count the number of nonnegative integer triples (a,b,c) corresponding to each feasible solution.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- Variables: Nonnegative integers a, b, c.
- Constraints:
  - Linear: a + b + c = 300.
  - Polynomial: a^2b + a^2c + b^2a + b^2c + c^2a + c^2b = 6,000,000.
- Objective: Find the number of triples (a,b,c) satisfying both constraints.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The sum constraint restricts the triples to a plane in the integer lattice.
- The polynomial is symmetric and homogeneous of degree 3, involving terms of the form a^2b and ab^2.
- The polynomial can be rewritten or related to symmetric sums or expressions involving a, b, c.
- The constraints together define a discrete set of points; the problem is combinatorial and algebraic.
- The polynomial condition likely restricts the distribution of values among a, b, c beyond just their sum.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- Primary domain: Combinatorics and Number Theory (integer solutions to Diophantine equations).
- Secondary domains: Algebra (symmetric polynomials), possibly discrete geometry.
- Contexts: Counting integer solutions under polynomial constraints is common in combinatorics and algebraic number theory, and appears in mathematical competitions.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The polynomial expression is symmetric but not obviously factorable; understanding its structure is key.
- No explicit ordering or distinctness conditions on (a,b,c) are given; all permutations count.
- Potential complexity arises from the large constants and the cubic nature of the polynomial.
- Assumptions: Treat a,b,c as independent nonnegative integers constrained only by the given equations; no further restrictions.
- Clarification on whether permutations of the same triple count separately is implied by the problem statement (likely yes).

This expression is symmetric in a, b, and c and consists of terms where one variable is squared and multiplied by another variable. To rewrite this in terms of symmetric sums, we first note that the expression can be grouped as a^2(b+c) + b^2(a+c) + c^2(a+b). Since a + b + c = 300, we can replace (b+c) by (300 - a), (a+c) by (300 - b), and (a+b) by (300 - c). Thus, the expression becomes a^2(300 - a) + b^2(300 - b) + c^2(300 - c) = 6,000,000. Expanding this, we get 300(a^2 + b^2 + c^2) - (a^3 + b^3 + c^3) = 6,000,000. Now, the problem reduces to expressing the sum of cubes and sum of squares in terms of symmetric sums. We know the elementary symmetric sums: S1 = a + b + c = 300, S2 = ab + bc + ca, and S3 = abc. The sum of squares can be expressed as a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = S1^2 - 2S2 = 300^2 - 2S2 = 90000 - 2S2. The sum of cubes a^3 + b^3 + c^3 can be expressed using the identity a^3 + b^3 + c^3 = S1^3 - 3S1S2 + 3S3 = 300^3 - 3*300*S2 + 3S3 = 27,000,000 - 900S2 + 3S3. Substituting these into the expanded polynomial expression, we have 300(90000 - 2S2) - (27,000,000 - 900S2 + 3S3) = 6,000,000. Simplifying, this becomes 27,000,000 - 600S2 - 27,000,000 + 900S2 - 3S3 = 6,000,000, which reduces to 300S2 - 3S3 = 6,000,000. Dividing both sides by 3, we get 100S2 - S3 = 2,000,000.     logs.append(subtask_desc_2_3)
    print("Step 2.3: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    final_answer = await self.make_final_answer(thinking_2_3_final, answer_2_3_final, sub_tasks, agents)
    return final_answer, logs
